Comment

тМКPartly metrical: vss. 15-17, 47-53, 55-70 are so reckoned by W. in the Index, p. 6.тМЛ Found also in the main in P─Бipp. xvi., but in the central parts with omissions and disorder of which the details are not given; тМКvss. 58, 60, 64-73 are wantingтМЛ. Not quoted at all by V─Бit., nor probably by K─Бu┼Ы., since ’the two Brahman-cow hymns’ mentioned in K─Бu┼Ы. 48. 13 are doubtless v. 18, 19; although the comm. тМКD─Бrila: cf. Ke┼Ыava, p. 35120тМЛ declares these тМКv. 18, 19тМЛ to constitute one of the ’two,’ and xii. 5 the other. *тМКThe Berlin ms. reads pr─Бguktarс╣гibrahmagav─лdevat─Бс╕е: so also SPP’s citation, Critical Notice, p. 21. This seems to mean that Ka┼Ыyapa is the с╣Ыс╣гi; h. 4 clearly has the same “deity” as this.тМЛ

Translations

Translated: Muir, i2. 288 (vss. 4-15); Ludwig, p. 529 (vss. 47-73); Henry, 209, 257; Griffith, ii. 127.

Griffith

On the duty of giving cows to Brahmans, and the sin and danger of withholding the gift

Translation
  1. By toil, by penance [is she] created, acquired by br├бhman,
    supported (┼Ыrit├б) on righteousness.
Notes

All our saс╣Бhit─Б-mss. combine vitt├б rt├й. The appearance of meter in
the verse (8 + 8) is perhaps not accidental; but there is no metrical
structure elsewhere in the section.

Translation
  1. All these depart from the Kshatriya who takes to himself the
    Brahman-cow, who scathes the Brahman.
Notes

abbreviates vs. 9 to ─Бyu┼Ы ca ┼Ыrotraс╣Б ca, and vs. 11 to t─Бni sarv─Бс╣Зy
apa kr─Бmanti kс╣гatriyasya. All our saс╣Бhit─Б-mss. read in vs. 10 ca
rt├бm. The Anukr. says of vss. 7-10, et─Б┼Ы catasraс╕е punaс╕е punaс╕е
pad─Бntareс╣Зa pad─Бbhy─Бs─Бd ekapad─Бс╕е: тМКthat is, they are 1-p. because
repeatedly or in each case the groups ending with ca have to be
recited with a p─Бda-interval, i.e. (as Dr. Ryder suggests) because there
is in each verse no main cesuraтМЛ.

[Pary─Бya III.тАФс╣гoс╕Нa┼Ыa. 12. vir─Бс╕Н viс╣гam─Б g─Бyatr─л; 13. ─Бsury

Griffith

All these blessings of a Kshatriya depart from him when he oppresseth the Brahman and taketh to himself the hhman’s cow.

    the god-reviler, in the shackle of death.

curiously enough. All our mss. have p├бс╕Нv-, and one or two -v─лс╣Е┼Ы- or
-viс╣Е┼Ы-. The verse admits of being read as a g─Бyatr─л, probably not by
accident, and might better have been printed as such.

Translation
  1. Let the sun thrust him forth from the sky, burn him down.

From heaven let Surya drive him and consume him.
